Please provide a value in [0,1] range.\"\n    42→        )\n    43→\n    44→    @torch.no_grad()\n    45→    def ema_update(ema_param_list: PARAM_LIST, current_param_list: PARAM_LIST, _):\n    46→        # foreach lerp only handles float and complex\n    47→        if torch.is_floating_point(ema_param_list[0]) or torch.is_complex(\n    48→            ema_param_list[0]\n    49→        ):\n    50→            torch._foreach_lerp_(ema_param_list, current_param_list, 1 - decay)\n    51→        else:\n    52→            for p_ema, p_model in zip(ema_param_list, current_param_list):\n    53→                p_ema.copy_(p_ema * decay + p_model * (1 - decay))\n    54→\n    55→    return ema_update\n    56→\n    57→\n    58→def get_swa_multi_avg_fn():\n    59→    \"\"\"Get the function applying stochastic weight average (SWA) across multiple params.\"\"\"\n    60→\n    61→    @torch.no_grad()\n    62→    def swa_update(\n    63→        averaged_param_list: PARAM_LIST,\n    64→        current_param_list: PARAM_LIST,\n    65→        num_averaged: Union[Tensor, int],\n    66→    ):\n    67→        # foreach lerp only handles float and complex\n    68→        if torch.is_floating_point(averaged_param_list[0]) or torch.is_complex(\n    69→            averaged_param_list[0]\n    70→        ):\n    71→            torch._foreach_lerp_(\n    72→                averaged_param_list,\n    73→                current_param_list,\n    74→                cast(float, 1 / (num_averaged + 1)),\n    75→            )\n    76→        else:\n    77→            diffs = torch._foreach_sub(current_param_list, averaged_param_list)\n    78→            if isinstance(num_averaged, Tensor):\n    79→                torch._foreach_addcdiv_(\n    80→                    averaged_param_list,\n    81→                    diffs,\n    82→                    [num_averaged + 1] * len(averaged_param_list),\n    83→                )\n    84→            else:\n    85→                torch._foreach_add_(\n    86→                    averaged_param_list, diffs, alpha=1.0 / (num_averaged + 1)\n    87→                )\n    88→\n    89→    return swa_update\n    90→\n    91→\n    92→def get_ema_avg_fn(decay=0.999):\n    93→    \"\"\"Get the function applying exponential moving average (EMA) across a single param.\"\"\"\n    94→\n    95→    if decay < 0.0 or decay > 1.0:\n    96→        raise ValueError(\n    97→            f\"Invalid decay value {decay} provided. Please provide a value in [0,1] range.\"\n    98→        )\n    99→\n   100→    @torch.no_grad()\n   101→    def ema_update(ema_param: Tensor, current_param: Tensor, num_averaged):\n   102→        return decay * ema_param + (1 - decay) * current_param\n   103→\n   104→    return ema_update\n   105→\n   106→\n   107→def get_swa_avg_fn():\n   108→    \"\"\"Get the function applying stochastic weight average (SWA) across a single param.\"\"\"\n   109→\n   110→    @torch.no_grad()\n   111→    def swa_update(\n   112→        averaged_param: Tensor, current_param: Tensor, num_averaged: Union[Tensor, int]\n   113→    ):\n   114→        return averaged_param + (current_param - averaged_param) / (num_averaged + 1)\n   115→\n   116→    return swa_update\n   117→\n   118→\n   119→class AveragedModel(Module):\n   120→    r\"\"\"Implements averaged model for Stochastic Weight Averaging (SWA) and Exponential Moving Average (EMA).\n   121→\n   122→    Stochastic Weight Averaging was proposed in `Averaging Weights Leads to\n   123→    Wider Optima and Better Generalization`_ by Pavel Izmailov, Dmitrii\n   124→    Podoprikhin, Timur Garipov, Dmitry Vetrov and Andrew Gordon Wilson\n   125→    (UAI 2018).\n   126→\n   127→    Exponential Moving Average is a variation of `Polyak averaging`_,\n   128→    but using exponential weights instead of equal weights across iterations.\n   129→\n   130→    AveragedModel class creates a copy of the provided module :attr:`model`\n   131→    on the device :attr:`device` and allows to compute running averages of the\n   132→    parameters of the :attr:`model`.\n   133→\n   134→    Args:\n   135→        model (torch.nn.Module): model to use with SWA/EMA\n   136→        device (torch.device, optional): if provided, the averaged model will be\n   137→            stored on the :attr:`device`\n   138→        avg_fn (function, optional): the averaging function used to update\n   139→            parameters; the function must take in the current value of the\n   140→            :class:`AveragedModel` parameter, the current value of :attr:`model`\n   141→            parameter, and the number of models already averaged; if None,\n   142→            an equally weighted average is used (default: None)\n   143→        multi_avg_fn (function, optional): the averaging function used to update\n   144→            parameters inplace; the function must take in the current values of the\n   145→            :class:`AveragedModel` parameters as a list, the current values of :attr:`model`\n   146→            parameters as a list, and the number of models already averaged; if None,\n   147→            an equally weighted average is used (default: None)\n   148→        use_buffers (bool): if ``True``, it will compute running averages for\n   149→            both the parameters and the buffers of the model. (default: ``False``)\n   150→\n   151→    Example:\n   152→        >>> # xdoctest: +SKIP(\"undefined variables\")\n   153→        >>> loader, optimizer, model, loss_fn = ...\n   154→        >>> swa_model = torch.optim.swa_utils.AveragedModel(model)\n   155→        >>> scheduler = torch.optim.lr_scheduler.CosineAnnealingLR(optimizer,\n   156→        >>>                                     T_max=300)\n   157→        >>> swa_start = 160\n   158→        >>> swa_scheduler = SWALR(optimizer, swa_lr=0.05)\n   159→        >>> for i in range(300):\n   160→        >>>      for input, target in loader:\n   161→        >>>          optimizer.zero_grad()\n   162→        >>>          loss_fn(model(input), target).backward()\n   163→        >>>          optimizer.step()\n   164→        >>>      if i > swa_start:\n   165→        >>>          swa_model.update_parameters(model)\n   166→        >>>          swa_scheduler.step()\n   167→        >>>      else:\n   168→        >>>          scheduler.step()\n   169→        >>>\n   170→        >>> # Update bn statistics for the swa_model at the end\n   171→        >>> torch.optim.swa_utils.update_bn(loader, swa_model)\n   172→\n   173→    You can also use custom averaging functions with the `avg_fn` or `multi_avg_fn` parameters.\n   174→    If no averaging function is provided, the default is to compute\n   175→    equally-weighted average of the weights (SWA).\n   176→\n   177→    Example:\n   178→        >>> # xdoctest: +SKIP(\"undefined variables\")\n   179→        >>> # Compute exponential moving averages of the weights and buffers\n   180→        >>> ema_model = torch.optim.swa_utils.AveragedModel(model,\n   181→        >>>             torch.optim.swa_utils.get_ema_multi_avg_fn(0.9), use_buffers=True)\n   182→\n   183→    .. note::\n   184→        When using SWA/EMA with models containing Batch Normalization you may\n   185→        need to update the activation statistics for Batch Normalization.\n   186→        This can be done either by using the :meth:`torch.optim.swa_utils.update_bn`\n   187→        or by setting :attr:`use_buffers` to `True`. The first approach updates the\n   188→        statistics in a post-training step by passing data through the model. The\n   189→        second does it during the parameter update phase by averaging all buffers.\n   190→        Empirical evidence has shown that updating the statistics in normalization\n   191→        layers increases accuracy, but you may wish to empirically test which\n   192→        approach yields the best results in your problem.\n   193→\n   194→    .. note::\n   195→        :attr:`avg_fn` and `multi_avg_fn` are not saved in the :meth:`state_dict` of the model.\n   196→\n   197→    .. note::\n   198→        When :meth:`update_parameters` is called for the first time (i.e.\n   199→        :attr:`n_averaged` is `0`) the parameters of `model` are copied\n   200→        to the parameters of :class:`AveragedModel`. For every subsequent\n   201→        call of :meth:`update_parameters` the function `avg_fn` is used\n   202→        to update the parameters.\n   203→\n   204→    .. _Averaging Weights Leads to Wider Optima and Better Generalization:\n   205→        https://arxiv.org/abs/1803.05407\n   206→    .. _There Are Many Consistent Explanations of Unlabeled Data: Why You Should\n   207→        Average:\n   208→        https://arxiv.org/abs/1806.05594\n   209→    .. _SWALP: Stochastic Weight Averaging in Low-Precision Training:\n   210→        https://arxiv.org/abs/1904.11943\n   211→    .. _Stochastic (default: \"cos\")\n   389→        last_epoch (int): the index of the last epoch (default: -1)\n   390→\n   391→    The :class:`SWALR` scheduler can be used together with other\n   392→    schedulers     >>> loader, optimizer, model = ...\n   398→        >>> lr_lambda = lambda epoch: 0.9\n   399→        >>> scheduler = torch.optim.lr_scheduler.MultiplicativeLR(optimizer,\n   400→        >>> 416→    \"\"\"\n   417→\n   418→    def __init__(\n   419→        self,\n   420→        optimizer: Optimizer,\n   421→        swa_lr: float,\n   422→        anneal_epochs=10,\n   423→ _linear_anneal(t):\n   447→        return t\n   448→\n   449→    @staticmethod\n   450→    def _cosine_anneal(t):\n   451→        return (1 - math.cos(math.pi * t)) / 2\n   452→\n   453→    @staticmethod\n   454→    def _get_initial_lr(lr, swa_lr, alpha):\n   455→        if alpha == 1:\n   456→            return swa_lr\n   457→        return (lr - alpha * swa_lr) / (1 - alpha)\n   458→\n   459→    def get_lr(self):\n   460→        \"\"\"Get learning rate.\"\"\"\n   461→        # `_get_lr_called_within_step` is only available `_enable_get_lr_call`,\n   462→        # so we ignore the See `LRScheduler.step()` for more details.\n   463→        if not self._get_lr_called_within_step:\n   464→            warnings.warn(\n   465→                \"To get the last learning rate computed by the scheduler, \"\n   466→                \"please use `get_last_lr()`.\",\n   467→                UserWarning,\n   468→            )\n   469→        # Set in `LRScheduler._initial_step()`\n   470→        step = self._step_count - 1\n   471→        if self.anneal_epochs == 0:\n   472→            step = max(1, step)\n   473→        prev_t = max(0, min(1, (step - 1) / max(1, self.anneal_epochs)))\n   474→        prev_alpha = self.anneal_func(prev_t)\n   475→        prev_lrs = [\n   476→            self._get_initial_lr(group[\"lr\"], group[\"swa_lr\"], prev_alpha)\n   477→            for group in self.optimizer.param_groups\n   478→        ]\n   479→        t = max(0, min(1, step / max(1, self.anneal_epochs)))\n   480→        alpha = self.anneal_func(t)\n   481→        return [\n   482→            group[\"swa_lr\"] * alpha + lr * (1 - alpha)\n   483→            for group, lr in zip(self.optimizer.param_groups, prev_lrs)\n   484→        ]\n   485→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. Please provide a value in [0,1] range.\"\n        )\n\n    @torch.no_grad()\n    def ema_update(ema_param_list: PARAM_LIST, current_param_list: PARAM_LIST, _):\n        # foreach lerp only handles float and complex\n        if torch.is_floating_point(ema_param_list[0]) or torch.is_complex(\n            ema_param_list[0]\n        ):\n            torch._foreach_lerp_(ema_param_list, current_param_list, 1 - decay)\n        else:\n            for p_ema, p_model in zip(ema_param_list, current_param_list):\n                p_ema.copy_(p_ema * decay + p_model * (1 - decay))\n\n    return ema_update\n\n\ndef get_swa_multi_avg_fn():\n    \"\"\"Get the function applying stochastic weight average (SWA) across multiple params.\"\"\"\n\n    @torch.no_grad()\n    def swa_update(\n        averaged_param_list: PARAM_LIST,\n        current_param_list: PARAM_LIST,\n        num_averaged: Union[Tensor, int],\n    ):\n        # foreach lerp only handles float and complex\n        if torch.is_floating_point(averaged_param_list[0]) or torch.is_complex(\n            averaged_param_list[0]\n        ):\n            torch._foreach_lerp_(\n                averaged_param_list,\n                current_param_list,\n                cast(float, 1 / (num_averaged + 1)),\n            )\n        else:\n            diffs = torch._foreach_sub(current_param_list, averaged_param_list)\n            if isinstance(num_averaged, Tensor):\n                torch._foreach_addcdiv_(\n                    averaged_param_list,\n                    diffs,\n                    [num_averaged + 1] * len(averaged_param_list),\n                )\n            else:\n                torch._foreach_add_(\n                    averaged_param_list, diffs, alpha=1.0 / (num_averaged + 1)\n                )\n\n    return swa_update\n\n\ndef get_ema_avg_fn(decay=0.999):\n    \"\"\"Get the function applying exponential moving average (EMA) across a single param.\"\"\"\n\n    if decay < 0.0 or decay > 1.0:\n        raise ValueError(\n            f\"Invalid decay value {decay} provided. Please provide a value in [0,1] range.\"\n        )\n\n    @torch.no_grad()\n    def ema_update(ema_param: Tensor, current_param: Tensor, num_averaged):\n        return decay * ema_param + (1 - decay) * current_param\n\n    return ema_update\n\n\ndef get_swa_avg_fn():\n    \"\"\"Get the function applying stochastic weight average (SWA) across a single param.\"\"\"\n\n    @torch.no_grad()\n    def swa_update(\n        averaged_param: Tensor, current_param: Tensor, num_averaged: Union[Tensor, int]\n    ):\n        return averaged_param + (current_param - averaged_param) / (num_averaged + 1)\n\n    return swa_update\n\n\nclass AveragedModel(Module):\n    r\"\"\"Implements averaged model for Stochastic Weight Averaging (SWA) and Exponential Moving Average (EMA).\n\n    Stochastic Weight Averaging was proposed in `Averaging Weights Leads to\n    Wider Optima and Better Generalization`_ by Pavel Izmailov, Dmitrii\n    Podoprikhin, Timur Garipov, Dmitry Vetrov and Andrew Gordon Wilson\n    (UAI 2018).\n\n    Exponential Moving Average is a variation of `Polyak averaging`_,\n    but using exponential weights instead of equal weights across iterations.\n\n    AveragedModel class creates a copy of the provided module :attr:`model`\n    on the device :attr:`device` and allows to compute running averages of the\n    parameters of the :attr:`model`.\n\n    Args:\n        model (torch.nn.Module): model to use with SWA/EMA\n        device (torch.device, optional): if provided, the averaged model will be\n            stored on the :attr:`device`\n        avg_fn (function, optional): the averaging function used to update\n            parameters; the function must take in the current value of the\n            :class:`AveragedModel` parameter, the current value of :attr:`model`\n            parameter, and the number of models already averaged; if None,\n            an equally weighted average is used (default: None)\n        multi_avg_fn (function, optional): the averaging function used to update\n            parameters inplace; the function must take in the current values of the\n            :class:`AveragedModel` parameters as a list, the current values of :attr:`model`\n            parameters as a list, and the number of models already averaged; if None,\n            an equally weighted average is used (default: None)\n        use_buffers (bool): if ``True``, it will compute running averages for\n            both the parameters and the buffers of the model. (default: ``False``)\n\n    Example:\n        >>> # xdoctest: +SKIP(\"undefined variables\")\n        >>> loader, optimizer, model, loss_fn = ...\n        >>> swa_model = torch.optim.swa_utils.AveragedModel(model)\n        >>> scheduler = torch.optim.lr_scheduler.CosineAnnealingLR(optimizer,\n        >>>                                     T_max=300)\n        >>> swa_start = 160\n        >>> swa_scheduler = SWALR(optimizer, swa_lr=0.05)\n        >>> for i in range(300):\n        >>>      for input, target in loader:\n        >>>          optimizer.zero_grad()\n        >>>          loss_fn(model(input), target).backward()\n        >>>          optimizer.step()\n        >>>      if i > swa_start:\n        >>>          swa_model.update_parameters(model)\n        >>>          swa_scheduler.step()\n        >>>      else:\n        >>>          scheduler.step()\n        >>>\n        >>> # Update bn statistics for the swa_model at the end\n        >>> torch.optim.swa_utils.update_bn(loader, swa_model)\n\n    You can also use custom averaging functions with the `avg_fn` or `multi_avg_fn` parameters.\n    If no averaging function is provided, the default is to compute\n    equally-weighted average of the weights (SWA).\n\n    Example:\n        >>> # xdoctest: +SKIP(\"undefined variables\")\n        >>> # Compute exponential moving averages of the weights and buffers\n        >>> ema_model = torch.optim.swa_utils.AveragedModel(model,\n        >>>             torch.optim.swa_utils.get_ema_multi_avg_fn(0.9), use_buffers=True)\n\n    .. note::\n        When using SWA/EMA with models containing Batch Normalization you may\n        need to update the activation statistics for Batch Normalization.\n        This can be done either by using the :meth:`torch.optim.swa_utils.update_bn`\n        or by setting :attr:`use_buffers` to `True`. The first approach updates the\n        statistics in a post-training step by passing data through the model. The\n        second does it during the parameter update phase by averaging all buffers.\n        Empirical evidence has shown that updating the statistics in normalization\n        layers increases accuracy, but you may wish to empirically test which\n        approach yields the best results in your problem.\n\n    .. note::\n        :attr:`avg_fn` and `multi_avg_fn` are not saved in the :meth:`state_dict` of the model.\n\n    .. note::\n        When :meth:`update_parameters` is called for the first time (i.e.\n        :attr:`n_averaged` is `0`) the parameters of `model` are copied\n        to the parameters of :class:`AveragedModel`. For every subsequent\n        call of :meth:`update_parameters` the function `avg_fn` is used\n        to update the parameters.\n\n    .. _Averaging Weights Leads to Wider Optima and Better activation\n    statistics for BatchNorm layers in the model.\n\n    Args:\n        loader (torch.utils.data.DataLoader): dataset loader to compute the\n            activation statistics on. update BatchNorm\n            statistics.\n        device (torch.device, optional): If set, data will be transferred to\n            :attr:`device` before being passed into :attr:`model`.\n\n    Example:\n        >>> # xdoctest: +SKIP(\"Undefined variables\")\n        >>> loader, model = ...\n        >>> torch.optim.swa_utils.update_bn(loader, model)\n\n    .. note::\n        The `update_bn` utility assumes that each data batch in :attr:`loader`\n        is either a tensor or a list or tuple of tensors; in the latter case it\n        is assumed that :meth:`model.forward()` should be called on the first\n        element of the list or tuple corresponding to the data batch.\n    \"\"\"\n    momenta = {}\n    for module in model.modules():\n        if isinstance(module, torch.nn.modules.batchnorm._BatchNorm):\n            module.reset_running_stats()\n            momenta[module] = module.momentum\n\n    if not momenta:\n        return\n\n    was_training = model.training\n    model.train()\n    for module in momenta.keys():\n        module.momentum = None\n\n    for input in loader:\n        if isinstance(input, (list, tuple)):\n            input = input[0]\n        if device is not None:\n            input = input.to(device)\n\n        model(input)\n\n    for bn_module in momenta.keys():\n        bn_module.momentum = momenta[bn_module]\n    model.train(was_training)\n\n\nclass SWALR(LRScheduler):\n    r\"\"\"Anneals the learning rate in each parameter group to a fixed value.\n\n    This learning rate scheduler is meant to be used with Stochastic Weight\n    Averaging (SWA) method (see `torch.optim.swa_utils.AveragedModel`).\n\n    Args:\n        optimizer (torch.optim.Optimizer): wrapped optimizer\n        swa_lrs (float or list): the learning rate value for all param groups\n            together or separately for each group.\n        annealing_epochs (int): number of epochs in the annealing phase\n            (default: 10)\n        annealing_strategy (str): \"cos\" or \"linear\"; specifies the annealing\n            strategy: \"cos\" for cosine annealing, \"linear\" for linear annealing\n            (default: \"cos\")\n        last_epoch (int): the index of the last epoch (default: -1)\n\n    The :class:`SWALR` scheduler can be used together with other\n    schedulers to switch to a constant learning rate late in the training\n    as in the example below.\n\n    Example:\n        >>> # xdoctest: +SKIP(\"Undefined variables\")\n        >>> loader, optimizer, model = ...\n        >>> lr_lambda = lambda epoch: 0.9\n        >>> scheduler = torch.optim.lr_scheduler.MultiplicativeLR(optimizer,\n        >>>        lr_lambda=lr_lambda)\n        >>> swa_scheduler = torch.optim.swa_utils.SWALR(optimizer,\n        >>>        anneal_strategy=\"linear\", anneal_epochs=20, swa_lr=0.05)\n        >>> swa_start = 160\n        >>> for i in range(300):\n        >>>      for input, target in loader:\n        >>>          optimizer.zero_grad()\n        >>>          loss_fn(model(input), target).backward()\n        >>>          optimizer.step()\n        >>>      if i > swa_start:\n        >>>          swa_scheduler.step()\n        >>>      else:\n        >>>          scheduler.step()\n\n    .. _Averaging Weights Leads to Wider Optima and Better Generalization:\n        https://arxiv.org/abs/1803.05407\n    \"\"\"\n\n    def __init__(\n        self,\n        optimizer: Optimizer,\n        swa_lr: float,\n        anneal_epochs=10,\n        anneal_strategy: Literal[\"cos\", \"linear\"] = \"cos\",\n        last_epoch=-1,\n    ):  # noqa: D107\n        swa_lrs = _format_param(\"swa_lr\", optimizer, swa_lr)\n        for swa_lr, group in zip(swa_lrs, optimizer.param_groups):\n            group[\"swa_lr\"] = swa_lr\n        if anneal_strategy not in [\"cos\", \"linear\"]:\n            raise ValueError(\n                \"anneal_strategy must by one of 'cos' or 'linear', \"\n                f\"instead got {anneal_strategy}\"\n            )\n        elif anneal_strategy == \"cos\":\n            self.anneal_func = self._cosine_anneal\n        elif anneal_strategy == \"linear\":\n            self.anneal_func = self._linear_anneal\n        if not isinstance(anneal_epochs, int) or anneal_epochs < 0:\n            raise ValueError(\n                f\"anneal_epochs must be equal or greater than 0, got {anneal_epochs}\"\n            )\n        self.anneal_epochs = anneal_epochs\n        super().__init__(optimizer, last_epoch)\n\n    @staticmethod\n    def _linear_anneal(t):\n        return t\n\n    @staticmethod\n    def _cosine_anneal(t):\n        return (1 - math.cos(math.pi * t)) / 2\n\n    @staticmethod\n    def _get_initial_lr(lr, swa_lr, alpha):\n        if alpha == 1:\n            return swa_lr\n        return (lr - alpha * swa_lr) / (1 - alpha)\n\n    def get_lr(self):\n        \"\"\"Get learning rate.\"\"\"\n        # `_get_lr_called_within_step` is only available `_enable_get_lr_call`,\n        # so we ignore the type error here. See `LRScheduler.step()` for more details.\n        if not self._get_lr_called_within_step:\n            warnings.warn(\n                \"To get the last learning rate computed by the scheduler, \"\n                \"please use `get_last_lr()`.\",\n                UserWarning,\n            )\n        # Set in `LRScheduler._initial_step()`\n        step = self._step_count - 1\n        if self.anneal_epochs == 0:\n            step = max(1, step)\n        prev_t = max(0, min(1, (step - 1) / max(1, self.anneal_epochs)))\n        prev_alpha = self.anneal_func(prev_t)\n        prev_lrs = [\n            self._get_initial_lr(group[\"lr\"], group[\"swa_lr\"], prev_alpha)\n            for group in self.optimizer.param_groups\n        ]\n        t = max(0, min(1, step / max(1, self.anneal_epochs)))\n        alpha = self.anneal_func(t)\n        return [\n            group[\"swa_lr\"] * alpha + lr * (1 - alpha)\n            for group, lr in zip(self.optimizer.param_groups, prev_lrs)\n        ]\n","numLines":485,"startLine":1,"totalLines":485}}}

technique described in \"Adding Gradient Noise Improves\n    Learning for Very Deep Networks\" (Zhu et al., 2018).\n\n    The noise variance follows a schedule: sigma^2 = eta / (1 + t)^gamma\n    where t is the step count, eta controls the initial noise magnitude,\n    and gamma controls the decay rate.\n\n    Args:\n        optimizer (torch.optim.Optimizer): The base optimizer to wrap\n        eta (float): Initial noise scale parameter (default: 0.01)\n        gamma (float): Noise decay exponent (default: 0.55)\n\n    Example:\n        >>> model = torch.nn.Linear(10, 2)\n        >>> loss.backward()\n        >>> optimizer.step()\n    \"\"\"\n\n    def __init__(\n        self,\n        optimizer: Optimizer,\n        eta: float = 0.01,\n        gamma: float = 0.55,\n    ):\n        r\"\"\"Initialize the GradientNoiseInjector.\n\n        Args:\n            optimizer: The base optimizer to wrap\n            eta: Initial noise scale (default: 0.01)\n            gamma: Noise decay \"eta\": self.eta,\n            \"gamma\": self.gamma,\n            \"step_count\": self.step_count,\n        }\n\n    def __setstate__(self, state):\n        self.optimizer = state[\"optimizer\"]\n        self.eta = state[\"eta\"]\n        self.gamma = state[\"gamma\"]\n        self.step_count = state[\"step_count\"]\n\n    @property\n    def param_groups(self):\n        \"\"\"Expose param_groups from the wrapped optimizer.\"\"\"\n        return self.optimizer.param_groups\n\n    @property\n    def state(self):\n        \"\"\"Expose state dict from the wrapped optimizer.\"\"\"\n        return \"\"\"Load state dict from the wrapped optimizer.\"\"\"\n        return self.optimizer.load_state_dict(state_dict)\n\n    def state_dict(self):\n        \"\"\"Get state dict from the wrapped Create a simple model\n        model = torch.nn.Linear(10, 5)\n        base_optimizer = SGD(model.parameters(), lr=0.1)\n        noise_optimizer = GradientNoiseInjector(base_optimizer, eta=0.1, gamma=0.55)\n\n        # Test initial noise variance\n        expected_variance_0 = eta / (1.0 + 0) ** gamma\n        expected_sigma_0 = expected_variance_0 ** 0.5\n        # After first step, step_count should be 1\n        # But we need to check it before the step increments it\n        self.assertEqual(noise_optimizer.step_count, 0)\n\n        # Create dummy input and target\n        x = torch.randn(4, 10)\n        y = torch.randn(4, 5)\n\n        for step in range(5):\n            output = model(x)\n            loss = torch.nn.functional.mse_loss(output, y)\n            loss.backward()\n\n            # Verify the wrapper delegates to SGD correctly\n        self.assertIs(noise_optimizer.optimizer, base_optimizer)\n        self.assertEqual(noise_optimizer.eta, 0.01)\n        self.assertEqual(noise_optimizer.gamma, 0.55)  #
